rowspan="2" style="width: 35%; border:solid 1px #fafafa; border-width:0 0 0 1px; text-align: center;">Surface\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background-color: #e6e6ff">\n<th style="width: 20%; border:solid 1px #fafafa; border-width:1px 1px 0 1px; text-align: center;">m\n</th>\n<th style="width: 20%; border:solid 1px #fafafa; border-width:1px 1px 0 1px; text-align: center;">ft\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align: center;">07L/25R\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;">3,600\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;">11,811\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;"><a href="/wiki/Asphalt" title="Asphalt">Asphalt</a>\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td style="text-align: center;">07R/25L\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;">4,000\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;">13,123\n</td>\n<td style="text-align: center;"><a href="/wiki/Concrete" title="Concrete">Concrete</a>\n</td></tr>\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n\n</tbody></table></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Berlin Brandenburg Airport <i>Willy Brandt</i></b> (<a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>: <i lang="de">Flughafen Berlin Brandenburg "Willy Brandt"</i>) (<a href="/wiki/IATA_airport_code" title="IATA airport code">IATA</a>: <b>BER</b>, <a href="/wiki/ICAO_airport_code" title="ICAO airport code">ICAO</a>: <b>EDDB</b>) is an <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">international airport</a> in <a href="/wiki/Sch%C3%B6nefeld" title="Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld">Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld</a>, just south of the <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> capital <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> in the state of <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg" title="Brandenburg">Brandenburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> Named after former <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_West_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayor of West Berlin">West Berlin mayor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany" title="Chancellor of Germany">West German chancellor</a> <a href="/wiki/Willy_Brandt" title="Willy Brandt">Willy Brandt</a>, it is located 18 kilometres (11&#160;mi) south-east of the city centre and serves as a base for <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>. It mostly features flights to European metropolitan and leisure destinations as well as a number of intercontinental services.\n</p><p>The new airport replaced nearby <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Sch%C3%B6nefeld_Airport" title="Berlin Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport">Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld</a> as well as <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tegel_Airport" title="Berlin Tegel Airport">Tegel</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tempelhof_Airport" title="Berlin Tempelhof Airport">Tempelhof</a> airports (with the latter closed in 2008) and became the single commercial airport serving Berlin and the surrounding <a href="/wiki/States_of_Germany" title="States of Germany">State</a> of <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg" title="Brandenburg">Brandenburg</a>, an area with a combined 6 million inhabitants. With projected annual passenger numbers of around 34 million,<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Berlin Brandenburg Airport is set to become the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Germany" title="List of the busiest airports in Germany">third busiest</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_airports_in_Germany" title="List of airports in Germany">airport in Germany</a> surpassing <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Airport" title="D\xc3\xbcsseldorf Airport">D\xc3\xbcsseldorf Airport</a> and making it one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_the_busiest_airports_in_Europe" title="List of the busiest airports in Europe">fifteen busiest</a> in Europe.\n</p><p>The airport was originally planned to open in October 2011, five years after starting construction in 2006. However, the project encountered a series of successive delays due to poor construction planning, execution, management, and corruption. Berlin Brandenburg Airport finally received its operational licence in May 2020,<sup id="cite_ref-license_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-license-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> and opened for commercial traffic on 31 October 2020, 14 years after construction started and 29 years after official planning was launched.<sup id="cite_ref-finaldate_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finaldate-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld\'s refurbished passenger facilities have been incorporated as <i>Terminal 5</i> as of 25 October 2020<sup id="cite_ref-SXFT5_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SXFT5-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> while all other airlines completed the transition from Tegel to Berlin Brandenburg Airport by 8 November 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-BERallocations_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BERallocations-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r886046785">.mw-parser-output .toclimit-2 .toclevel-1 .toclimit-7 .toclevel-6 ul{display:none}</style><div class="toclimit-4"><div id="toc" class="toc" role="navigation" aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading"><input type="checkbox" role="button" class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Plans_for_a_new_Berlin_Airport">Plans for a new Berlin Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Plans for a new Berlin Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tupolev_Tu-134A-3,_CCCP-65783,_Aeroflot.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Tupolev_Tu-134A-3%2C_CCCP-65783%2C_Aeroflot.jpg/220px-Tupolev_Tu-134A-3%2C_CCCP-65783%2C_Aeroflot.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Tupolev_Tu-134A-3%2C_CCCP-65783%2C_Aeroflot.jpg/330px-Tupolev_Tu-134A-3%2C_CCCP-65783%2C_Aeroflot.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Tupolev_Tu-134A-3%2C_CCCP-65783%2C_Aeroflot.jpg/440px-Tupolev_Tu-134A-3%2C_CCCP-65783%2C_Aeroflot.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="681" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tupolev_Tu-134A-3,_CCCP-65783,_Aeroflot.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A view of the apron of <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Sch%C3%B6nefeld_Airport" title="Berlin Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport">Berlin Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport</a> (1990)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_Berlin-Schoenefeld_Airport_SFX_with_planed_BBI.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Map_Berlin-Schoenefeld_Airport_SFX_with_planed_BBI.png/220px-Map_Berlin-Schoenefeld_Airport_SFX_with_planed_BBI.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Map_Berlin-Schoenefeld_Airport_SFX_with_planed_BBI.png/330px-Map_Berlin-Schoenefeld_Airport_SFX_with_planed_BBI.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Map_Berlin-Schoenefeld_Airport_SFX_with_planed_BBI.png/440px-Map_Berlin-Schoenefeld_Airport_SFX_with_planed_BBI.png 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="2264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_Berlin-Schoenefeld_Airport_SFX_with_planed_BBI.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing the infrastructure of the Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld area and the relationship between the new and old airports</div></div></div>\n<p>After the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a> in 1989, and following <a href="/wiki/German_reunification" title="German reunification">German reunification</a> in 1990, Berlin once again became the German federal capital; leaders made plans to recognise the city\'s increased importance by constructing a large commercial airport. Existing airports <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tegel_Airport" title="Berlin Tegel Airport">Tegel Airport</a>, <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Sch%C3%B6nefeld_Airport" title="Berlin Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport">Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tempelhof_Airport" title="Berlin Tempelhof Airport">Tempelhof Airport</a> were ageing and becoming increasingly congested due to rising passenger numbers. To ensure the economic viability of the project, they pursued the <i>single airport concept</i>, meaning that the new airport would become the sole commercial airport for Berlin and Brandenburg. They planned to close Tegel, Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld and Tempelhof upon opening the new airport, then ban commercial aviation from any other airport in Brandenburg.\n</p><p>On 2 May 1991, the <i><a href="/wiki/Flughafen_Berlin_Brandenburg_GmbH" title="Flughafen Berlin Brandenburg GmbH">Berlin Brandenburg Flughafen Holding GmbH</a></i> (BBF) was founded, owned by the states of Berlin and Brandenburg (37 per cent each) and the Federal Republic of Germany (the remaining 26 per cent). <a href="/wiki/Eberhard_Diepgen" title="Eberhard Diepgen">Eberhard Diepgen</a>, Mayor of Berlin, became the first chairman of the supervisory board.  The holding company announced on 20 June 1993 that <a href="/wiki/Sperenberg_Airfield" title="Sperenberg Airfield">Sperenberg Airfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCterbog_Airfield" title="J\xc3\xbcterbog Airfield">J\xc3\xbcterbog Airfield</a> and the area south of Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport, where the evaluation of the locations Sperenberg, J\xc3\xbcterbog East, J\xc3\xbcterbog West, Tietzow, Michelsdorf, Borkheide and Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld South was carried out according to five criteria with different weighting. Each site was advocated by various factions in the ensuing political discussion.<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> With regard to <a href="/wiki/Land-use_planning" title="Land-use planning">land-use planning</a> and <a href="/wiki/Noise_pollution" title="Noise pollution">noise pollution</a>, rural Sperenberg and J\xc3\xbcterbog were considered more suitable for construction of a large airport. Economic considerations favoured an airport located near the city center, with existing road and rail links (as it is the case with Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld).<sup id="cite_ref-timeline_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-timeline-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 May 1996 Mayor Diepgen, Minister-President of Brandenburg <a href="/wiki/Manfred_Stolpe" title="Manfred Stolpe">Manfred Stolpe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_of_Transport,_Building_and_Urban_Development" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Ministry of Transport, Building and Urban Development">Federal Minister for Transport</a> <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Wissmann" title="Matthias Wissmann">Matthias Wissmann</a> committed to Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld as the site for the new airport. This so-called <i>consensus decision</i> was later affirmed by the respective state legislatures.<sup id="cite_ref-consensus_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-consensus-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> The new airport would use some infrastructure, such as a runway, from the current Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Failed_privatisation">Failed privatisation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Failed privatisation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Originally, BBF hoped the new airport would be owned and operated by a private investor. They called for proposals, which led to two bidding consortia emerging as serious contenders. One was led by <a href="/wiki/Hochtief" title="Hochtief">Hochtief</a> through its <a href="/wiki/Hochtief_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Hochtief Airport">Hochtief Airport</a> subsidiary and included <a href="/wiki/ABB_Group" class="mw-redirect" title="ABB Group">ABB</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fraport" title="Fraport">Fraport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Landesbank_Berlin_Holding" title="Landesbank Berlin Holding">Bankengesellschaft Berlin</a> as partners.  The other consortium comprised <a href="/wiki/IVG_Immobilien" title="IVG Immobilien">IVG</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Vienna Airport">Flughafen Wien AG</a>, Dorsch-Consult, <a href="/wiki/Commerzbank" title="Commerzbank">Commerzbank</a> and <a href="/wiki/Caisse_des_d%C3%A9p%C3%B4ts_et_consignations" title="Caisse des d\xc3\xa9p\xc3\xb4ts et consignations">Caisse des D\xc3\xa9p\xc3\xb4ts</a>. On 19 September 1998, BBF announced that the Hochtief consortium were the successful bidder. This saw them granted exclusive authority to negotiate the terms and conditions for an acquisition of the Berlin Brandenburg Airport holding and the construction and operation of the new airport for 50 years.<sup id="cite_ref-welt_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-welt-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 31 March 1999, BBF officially commissioned Hochtief and its partners to construct the new airport, causing IVG to file a lawsuit. The Brandenburg <a href="/wiki/Oberlandesgericht" title="Oberlandesgericht">Oberlandesgericht</a> acknowledged the concerns voiced by IVG. In its review, it found that in certain points the assessment of the applications had been biased towards Hochtief. This led to annulment of the <a href="/wiki/Contract_awarding" title="Contract awarding">contract award</a> on 3 August of that year.<sup id="cite_ref-neumann_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neumann-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Hochtief Airport and IVG teamed up and created a plan for a joint bid on 10 November 2000 in an attempt to receive the contract to construct and operate the new airport.<sup id="cite_ref-hochtief10Nov_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hochtief10Nov-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> At the time BBF hoped that the planning approval could be completed in 2002, with the tentative opening in 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-handelsblatt_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-handelsblatt-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When Hochtief/IVG submitted its bid in February 2002, the BBF board consisted of Manfred Stolpe, now Federal Minister of Transportation; <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Wowereit" title="Klaus Wowereit">Klaus Wowereit</a>, who replaced Eberhard Diepgen as Mayor of Berlin and chair of the board; and <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Platzeck" title="Matthias Platzeck">Matthias Platzeck</a>, who replaced Stolpe as Minister-President of Brandenburg. The board determined that the proposal would not be practical and voted 22 May 2003 to scrap the privatisation plan.<sup id="cite_ref-allgemeine_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-allgemeine-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> Hochtief and IVG received approximately \xe2\x82\xac50 million compensation for their planning effort.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_ownership_and_construction_permit">Public ownership and construction permit</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Public ownership and construction permit">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The new Berlin airport would be planned, owned and operated by BBF Holding. Shortly afterwards BBF Holding became <i>Flughafen Berlin Brandenburg GmbH</i> (FBB) and remained under the ownership of Berlin, Brandenburg and the federal government. On 13 August 2004, the Brandenburg state ministry for infrastructure and regional policy granted approval for the development of Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport into new Berlin Brandenburg International Airport.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A legal battle ensued, as local residents filed lawsuits against the ministry\'s decision. The dispute ended 16 March 2006, when the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Administrative_Court_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Administrative Court of Germany">Federal Administrative Court of Germany</a> rejected the residents\' arguments. However, the court imposed stipulations on the flight operations at the new airport.<sup id="cite_ref-soar_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-soar-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Construction_permit" class="mw-redirect" title="Construction permit">construction permit</a> was granted only under the condition that once operational, the number of people living in the approach path would be lower compared to the situation surrounding the three existing airports \xe2\x80\x93 Tegel, Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld and Tempelhof.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Therefore, it was mandatory for Tegel and Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld to close (Tempelhof was already decommissioned in 2008) once Berlin\'s air traffic was concentrated at the new airport.<sup id="cite_ref-court_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-court-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Financing">Financing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Financing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>By 2009 the construction cost was budgeted at \xe2\x82\xac2.83 billion. FBB raised the financing for the project by a credit raising of \xe2\x82\xac2.4 billion, a bank deposit of \xe2\x82\xac430 million by the FBB partners and an additional \xe2\x82\xac440 million of equity capital provided by FBB.<sup id="cite_ref-neumann02_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-neumann02-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During construction, it became clear that the airport would become significantly more expensive due to underestimating the actual costs, construction flaws and increased expenses for soundproofing nearby homes. As of 2012, the series of delays in opening was expected to lead to a number of lawsuits against FBB with now defunct <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a> announcing its intentions of such a move.<sup id="cite_ref-spiegelNov12_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegelNov12-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By late 2012 expenditures for Berlin Brandenburg Airport totalled \xe2\x82\xac4.3 billion, more than half as much again as the originally anticipated figure.<sup id="cite_ref-spiegelJan13_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegelJan13-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It became clear in November 2015 that the financial concept of the airport will remain fundamentally flawed. The main purpose of the many stores planned at the airport was to serve passengers who were changing planes, assuming that Berlin would be a big international hub. However, it was acknowledged in 2015 for the first time that competition between the hubs was already too stiff. <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow</a> would resist losing passenger shares without a price war and that few if any airlines would leave their hubs for Berlin. The only remaining potential airline for operating a hub was Air Berlin, which was in financial difficulties and did not plan to provide long-distance service anytime soon.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>German Railways <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> also sued for non-usage of the <a href="/wiki/Ghost_station" title="Ghost station">ghost station</a> below the airport as of 2012<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> with the airport having to pay damages as of May 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2015, auditors with the <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg" title="Brandenburg">Brandenburg</a> <a href="/wiki/Comptroller" title="Comptroller">Comptroller</a> concluded that financial control executed by <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg" title="Brandenburg">Brandenburg</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> over the airport as owners was insufficient and inefficient.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> The Comptroller published a 400-page report in February 2016 describing the flawed opening including several construction lapses. This led the BER boss to retaliate publicly against the comptroller on 27 February decrying the release of the numbers.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Soundproofing" title="Soundproofing">Soundproofing</a> nearby homes will be \xe2\x82\xac50<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million more expensive due to a verdict of the main administrative courts of the states of <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg" title="Brandenburg">Brandenburg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> As of 5 May 2016 the court decided in favour of 25,500 plaintiffs. See also: <a href="/wiki/Federal_Administrative_Court_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Administrative Court of Germany">Federal Administrative Court of Germany</a>. The key directive of the verdict was that rooms must be provided with adequate ventilation if windows are closed due to noise, and the airport authority must also determine how air inside the structures can be vented. The airport avoided liability claims against Imtech and other firms involved in the construction of the fire exhaustion system.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Financing for the entire airport appeared headed toward bankruptcy in June 2016 due to the EU\'s unwillingness to approve a pending request for \xe2\x82\xac2.5<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion bringing the project to \xe2\x82\xac6.9<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion. If the request was denied, the airport authority stated it would be bankrupt by August 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The EU permitted an additional \xe2\x82\xac2.2<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion on 3 August 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-tagesspiegel.de_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tagesspiegel.de-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> A \xe2\x82\xac2.4&#160;billion loan was signed on 13 February 2017 containing \xe2\x82\xac1.1 billion for financing and \xe2\x82\xac1.3 billion to resolve old bad loans. The German federal government and the states of Berlin and Brandenburg guaranteed the debt.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of 2015, total costs amounted to \xe2\x82\xac5.4&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Revised plans suggest additional costs amounting to an extra \xe2\x82\xac2.19&#160;billion. As of 3 June 2015, Germany applied for an additional \xe2\x82\xac2.5 billion spending approval from the EU. This is in addition to the previous total of \xe2\x82\xac4.3&#160;billion, bringing total costs to \xe2\x82\xac6.8 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The EU would only permit an additional \xe2\x82\xac2.2 billion, which it did on 3 August 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-tagesspiegel.de_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tagesspiegel.de-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> Although the airport has yet to open officials are planning a possible third runway for approximately \xe2\x82\xac1 billion and other new projects such as an additional terminal, expanded baggage system and another freight facility. The total additional spending would amount to \xe2\x82\xac3.2&#160;billion.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The board warned of a further rise in costs because the airport will not open before 2017. The current time-cost frame is limited to 2016;<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> the estimated cost of \xe2\x82\xac6.9&#160;billion is current as of May 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> The airport company reportedly made the assurance to the <a href="/wiki/European_Investment_Bank" title="European Investment Bank">European Investment Bank</a> that the airport will open in September 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Forecasts estimate the airport will not be ready to open until 2020. This means a need for \xe2\x82\xac500 million for refinancing to bridge the time gap between 2019 and 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-focus_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-focus-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> The airport published a need for another billion euros up until 2020. This means that the three years of work from 2018 onwards will cost at least \xe2\x82\xac900 million.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The total cost of the airport will top \xe2\x82\xac6.5 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of 13 January 2018, the company requested an additional \xe2\x82\xac2.8 billion for extensions until 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> Taking that into account, the total cost comes to \xe2\x82\xac9.4 billion,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> with a total of \xe2\x82\xac10.3 billion if the \xe2\x82\xac900 million in overhead costs previously mentioned are factored in. An economical estimate determined the costs for the overheads at a conservative figure of \xe2\x82\xac770 million.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The airport is planning to borrow \xe2\x82\xac400 million.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Another issue arose when it became public that the airport head earns an annual salary of \xe2\x82\xac500,000.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> A new loan was granted by the German parliament on 30 June 2018 totalling \xe2\x82\xac132 million. The other two owners, the states of Brandenburg and Berlin, will likely permit their shares of the loan as well, so the loan will total \xe2\x82\xac500 million.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> The board postponed a decision concerning the loan until the end of August 2018, which leaves the entire finance planning in jeopardy.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> At the end of August 2018 Berlin\'s head of finance, Matthias Kollatz, made the remark that the airport may face abrupt bankruptcy on 1 January 2019, if no instant measures would be taken.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> The financial head resigned from the holding company of Berlin\'s airports at the end of September 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> According to projections the airport is in dire need of additional \xe2\x82\xac508 million from 2021 onwards.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> There seems to be another need for financial support from authorities for the next 2 years as of 29 April 2020 amounting to \xe2\x82\xac1.8 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> A new study claimed that the net worth of the current building is far lower than the credited \xe2\x82\xac4,866 million and it is to be settled at \xe2\x82\xac3 billion less.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> The financial gap due to the COVID-19 pandemic is estimated to be at \xe2\x82\xac300&#160;million for Tegel and Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld combined, thus the new airport will be in need for financial support for years to come.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The annual manager report of 2019 of BER\'s operating firm was criticised by Linkspartei as extremely short and intransparent.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Cash flow concerns amount to a dire need of \xe2\x82\xac1.5 billion as of immediate in 20 June.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 13 July 2020, prosecutors filed a complaint on suspicion of falsifying the balance sheet. The financial auditors for FBB were the same as for the now insolvent <a href="/wiki/Wirecard" title="Wirecard">Wirecard</a> company, raising doubts about the validity of the audits.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The plan to generate profits starting in 2023/2024 has been overturned by the COVID-19 pandemic according to airport head Engelbert L\xc3\xbctke-Daldrup (<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Engelbert_L%C3%BCtke-Daldrup" class="extiw" title="de:Engelbert L\xc3\xbctke-Daldrup">de</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>There seems to be a demand of \xe2\x82\xac375 million for 2021 to cover current costs for BER, the parent company announced on 9 October 2020. An additional \xe2\x82\xac552 million are needed as a stabilization for missing passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Naming">Naming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Naming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F057884-0009,_Willy_Brandt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F057884-0009%2C_Willy_Brandt.jpg/150px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F057884-0009%2C_Willy_Brandt.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F057884-0009%2C_Willy_Brandt.jpg/225px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F057884-0009%2C_Willy_Brandt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F057884-0009%2C_Willy_Brandt.jpg/300px-Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F057884-0009%2C_Willy_Brandt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="552" data-file-height="776" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bundesarchiv_B_145_Bild-F057884-0009,_Willy_Brandt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The airport is named after Nobel Peace Laureate <a href="/wiki/Willy_Brandt" title="Willy Brandt">Willy Brandt</a>, former <a href="/wiki/Mayor_of_Berlin" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayor of Berlin">Mayor</a> of <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany_(Federal_Republic_of_Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chancellor of Germany (Federal Republic of Germany)">Chancellor of West Germany</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>During much of the planning and construction phase the new airport was known as <b>Berlin Brandenburg International Airport</b>, abbreviated <b>BBI.</b> It was then discovered that the <a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" class="mw-redirect" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">IATA code</a> <b>BBI</b> already referred to <a href="/wiki/Biju_Patnaik_Airport" title="Biju Patnaik Airport">Biju Patnaik Airport</a> (also known as Bhubaneswar Airport) in India. When the planned opening date of 2 June 2012 drew nearer the FBB launched a marketing campaign introducing the <b>BER</b> branding, reflecting the new <a href="/wiki/International_Air_Transport_Association_airport_code" class="mw-redirect" title="International Air Transport Association airport code">airport code</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2007 the FBB board decided that Berlin Brandenburg Airport would be given a second name, honouring a person with a distinctive link to the city of Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-airportname_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airportname-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> On 11 December 2009, the decision was made in favour of <a href="/wiki/Willy_Brandt" title="Willy Brandt">Willy Brandt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-beiklerkurpjuweit_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-beiklerkurpjuweit-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace</a> laureate of 1971 served as mayor of <a href="/wiki/West_Berlin" title="West Berlin">West Berlin</a> from 1957 to 1966 and as <a href="/wiki/Chancellor_of_Germany_(Federal_Republic_of_Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Chancellor of Germany (Federal Republic of Germany)">West German chancellor</a> from 1969 to 1974. Berlin mayor <a href="/wiki/Klaus_Wowereit" title="Klaus Wowereit">Klaus Wowereit</a> and Minister-President of Brandenburg <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Platzeck" title="Matthias Platzeck">Matthias Platzeck</a>, both members of the <a href="/wiki/Social_Democratic_Party_of_Germany" title="Social Democratic Party of Germany">Social Democratic Party of Germany</a> (SPD) (which Brandt led from 1964 to 1987) led the effort to add Brandt\'s name to the airport.\n</p><p>Other suggested honorees included <a href="/wiki/Claus_Schenk_Graf_von_Stauffenberg" class="mw-redirect" title="Claus Schenk Graf von Stauffenberg">Claus Schenk Graf von Stauffenberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marlene_Dietrich" title="Marlene Dietrich">Marlene Dietrich</a> (suggested by members of the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Democratic_Union_(Germany)" class="mw-redirect" title="Christian Democratic Union (Germany)">Christian Democratic Union</a>), <a href="/wiki/Gustav_Stresemann" title="Gustav Stresemann">Gustav Stresemann</a> (nominated by the <a href="/wiki/Free_Democratic_Party_(Germany)" title="Free Democratic Party (Germany)">Free Democratic Party</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Otto_Lilienthal" title="Otto Lilienthal">Otto Lilienthal</a> (advocated by the <a href="/wiki/Alliance_%2790/The_Greens" class="mw-redirect" title="Alliance &#39;90/The Greens">Green Party</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-airportname_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airportname-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As a result of the ongoing problems affecting the airport and the continuous negative publicity it got in the German and international press, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bundeskanzler-Willy-Brandt-Stiftung&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bundeskanzler-Willy-Brandt-Stiftung (page does not exist)">Willy Brandt Foundation</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bundeskanzler-Willy-Brandt-Stiftung" class="extiw" title="de:Bundeskanzler-Willy-Brandt-Stiftung">de</a>&#93;</span> considered revoking the airport\'s permission to bear the former chancellor\'s name. This is due to concerns that an ongoing association might be considered disrespectful towards his legacy. However, no such measure has been taken so far.<sup id="cite_ref-Spiegel2013_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spiegel2013-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Construction_progress_and_issues">Construction progress and issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Construction progress and issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The construction of Berlin Brandenburg Airport suffered from continued delays which were caused by an array of issues.\n</p><p>The most significant cause for the continuing delays was the fire protection and alarm system. In the terminal building, the system was not built according to the <a href="/wiki/Construction_permit" class="mw-redirect" title="Construction permit">construction permit</a> and failed the <a href="/wiki/Technischer_%C3%9Cberwachungsverein" title="Technischer \xc3\x9cberwachungsverein">mandatory acceptance test</a> necessary to open the airport. FBB proposed an interim solution employing up to 700 human fire spotters, which the building supervision department of the local <a href="/wiki/Dahme-Spreewald" title="Dahme-Spreewald">Dahme-Spreewald</a> district rejected.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Inspectors uncovered flaws in the wiring, programming and implementation of the highly complex system designed by <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bosch_GmbH" title="Robert Bosch GmbH">Bosch</a>. The system automatically controls sprinklers, smoke extractors and fire doors.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> For aesthetic reasons, designers decided that the terminal would have smoke extraction ducts in its ceiling but that they would not exhaust to its rooftop. During a fire, smoke would be pumped from the ceiling into a shaft running down and through the basement <i>below</i> the structure.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> This required the natural rising behaviour of hot air in the shaft to be reversed. Achieving this on the scale necessary for this airport is a unique undertaking and so far this elaborate smoke extraction system has not worked as planned.<sup id="cite_ref-spiegelJan13_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegelJan13-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> To meet the acceptance test requirements, large scale reconstruction work of the fire system might be needed.<sup id="cite_ref-failures_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-failures-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> It emerged that Alfredo di Mauro, who designed the fire safety system, was not a qualified engineer. While his business cards stated he was an engineer, he was actually qualified as an engineering <a href="/wiki/Drafter" title="Drafter">draughtsman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> Di Mauro was dismissed by the airport company in early May 2014. In the termination notice, the company cited "serious defects" in his work and that trust in their relationship was "now finally shattered". The airport company went on to state that Di Mauro\'s plans would be "disposed of". The system was to be rebuilt and divided into three areas in order to make it "manageable". The cost of this work was reported as being a nine-digit figure.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Another major factor impacting on the construction of the airport was insolvency of general planner <i>Planungsgemeinschaft Flughafen Berlin Brandenburg International</i> (pg bbi) and the dismissal of the <a href="/wiki/Gerkan,_Marg_and_Partners" title="Gerkan, Marg and Partners">Gerkan, Marg and Partners</a> architects. Inspectors have uncovered many examples of poor workmanship due to a lack of proper supervision and documentation, most notably concerning the wiring. Reports have surfaced about cable conduits that hold too many cables or hold cables in incompatible combinations, such as phone lines next to high voltage wires. A total of 60 kilometres (37&#160;mi) of cooling pipes were allegedly installed with no thermal insulation. To correct this, the demolition of numerous walls may be necessary. Furthermore, exterior vents appear to be in improper locations, allowing rainwater from the western facade to enter them.<sup id="cite_ref-failures_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-failures-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline">Timeline</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Timeline">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; margin-left:1em">\n<caption>Construction delays<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Announcement</th>\n<th>Opening date\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>5 September 2006 (original)</td>\n<td>30 October 2011\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>25 June 2010</td>\n<td>3 June 2012\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>7 May 2012</td>\n<td>17 March 2013\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>27 October 2012</td>\n<td>27 October 2013\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>January 2013</td>\n<td>on/after 2014\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>8 January 2014</td>\n<td>on/after 2015\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>24 February 2014</td>\n<td>on/after 2016\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>14 May 2014</td>\n<td>on/after 2017\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>December 2014</td>\n<td>2nd half of 2017\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>21 January 2017</td>\n<td>2018\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>15 December 2017</td>\n<td>31 October 2020\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2006">2006</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2006">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>After nearly 15 years of planning, actual construction work for Berlin Brandenburg Airport began on 5 September 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-groundbreaking_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-groundbreaking-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> When construction began, FBB announced 30 October 2011 as the opening day for the new facility.<sup id="cite_ref-schedule_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schedule-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> To make way for the new airport, two villages were removed. The 335 inhabitants of Diepensee received compensation and were offered new homes in <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6nigs_Wusterhausen" title="K\xc3\xb6nigs Wusterhausen">K\xc3\xb6nigs Wusterhausen</a>, a move that was completed by late 2004. The 35 villagers of Selchow were resettled to <a href="/wiki/Buckow_(Berlin)" title="Buckow (Berlin)">Gro\xc3\x9fziethen</a> in mid-2005.<sup id="cite_ref-history_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-presskit_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-presskit-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>16</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2007">2007</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2007">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In November 2007, the <i>BER-Infotower</i> opened a 32-metre-high (105&#160;ft) public observation tower and information center.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> It was part of the airport\'s visitor facilities, which also had a webcam of the construction progress.<sup id="cite_ref-infotower2_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infotower2-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> The transparent and twisted structure was originally intended to be temporary, with a scheduled removal announced in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Abgerissen_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abgerissen-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2008">2008</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 2008">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>Construction of the terminal building began in July 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-jacobs_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-jacobs-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2010">2010</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 2010">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BBI_2010-07-23_3.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/BBI_2010-07-23_3.JPG/220px-BBI_2010-07-23_3.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/BBI_2010-07-23_3.JPG/330px-BBI_2010-07-23_3.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/BBI_2010-07-23_3.JPG/440px-BBI_2010-07-23_3.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1920" data-file-height="1080" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BBI_2010-07-23_3.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Construction progress at today\'s Terminal 1 as of 2010</div></div></div>\n<p>On 8 and 9 May 2010, the airport celebrated its <a href="/wiki/Topping_out" title="Topping out">topping out</a> with open days at the airport site.<sup id="cite_ref-topping_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-topping-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> A few days after 14 June 2010 topping out ceremony, FBB announced that construction deadlines could not be met. They postponed the opening to 3 June 2012. This was blamed on the bankruptcy of <i>IGK-IGR</i>, which was part of the <i>pg bbi</i> construction planning company.<sup id="cite_ref-fulling_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fulling-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2011">2011</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 2011">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 30 October 2011, the railway line and <a href="/wiki/BER_Airport_%E2%80%93_Terminal_1-2_station" title="BER Airport \xe2\x80\x93 Terminal 1-2 station">terminal station</a> were ready for service, however no scheduled trains will operate until the opening.\n</p><p>Operating tests and service trials began on 24 November 2011, based on the anticipated opening date of 3 June 2012. A total of 12,000 volunteers participated in simulated check-in, security screening, boarding and baggage claim. The tests used 15,000 pieces of luggage in the <a href="/wiki/Baggage_handling_system" title="Baggage handling system">automated baggage processing system</a>, covered night-time operations and emergency scenarios.<sup id="cite_ref-2011report_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011report-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> This phase also saw the acceptance tests of various airport systems. It became clear on 8 May 2012 that the building could not open on schedule, officially due to the failure of the fire protection system. In reality, according to a Brandenburg State Audit report in February 2016 the usability of the airport was at 56.2%; for example, there were no ticket counters and the escalators did not work. The report went on to say there was no realistic chance that it could be used "reasonably successfully" in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-SpiegelFeb2016_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SpiegelFeb2016-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> Legal implications concerning the failed 2012 opening are likely following the publication of the 2016 report.<sup id="cite_ref-DiepgenMomper_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DiepgenMomper-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2012">2012</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 2012">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>As the new date drew nearer, airlines amended their timetables to reflect their plans to operate from BER. On the retail side of the airport, shops and restaurants prepared for the opening. As the airports in Tegel and Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld were to close once the last flights of 2 June had been serviced, a major logistics operation for moving the airports\' infrastructure was launched. Vehicles, equipment and supplies that were needed at Tegel until the final moments would have been transported to BER during the night of 2\xe2\x80\x933 June. To allow this, the authorities planned to restrict the highways linking the two airports (<a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_113" title="Bundesautobahn 113">A113</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_100" title="Bundesautobahn 100">A100</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Bundesautobahn_111" title="Bundesautobahn 111">A111</a>) to airport traffic only.<sup id="cite_ref-megamove_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-megamove-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rundfunk_Berlin_Brandenburg" class="mw-redirect" title="Rundfunk Berlin Brandenburg">Rundfunk Berlin Brandenburg</a>, the national broadcaster for Berlin and Brandenburg, scheduled 24 hours of continuous live coverage of the airport move.<sup id="cite_ref-rbb_102-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rbb-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> A special Lufthansa flight to <a href="/wiki/Frankfurt_Airport" title="Frankfurt Airport">Frankfurt Airport</a>, operated with an <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>, was scheduled as the first departure from the new airport on 3 June at 06:00.<sup id="cite_ref-rbb_102-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rbb-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 8 May 2012 just 26 days before the move, FBB again postponed the opening date. The postponement led to the cancelling of moving plans and in some cases reversing actions already completed. It cited technical difficulties, primarily concerning the fire safety and smoke exhaust systems for the delay.<sup id="cite_ref-Further_Delay_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Further_Delay-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> As a result, FBB dismissed the director for technical affairs Manfred K\xc3\xb6rtgen and replaced him with Horst Amann. It also announced 17 March 2013 as the new opening date for BER. However, this was soon met by doubts due to the large number of construction flaws and problems that inspectors continued to find.<sup id="cite_ref-gubisch_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gubisch-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In early September 2012, FBB further postponed the opening to 27 October 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-spiegel0409_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegel0409-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Again, media and experts (most notably <a href="/wiki/Peter_Ramsauer" title="Peter Ramsauer">Peter Ramsauer</a>, Federal Minister for Construction and Infrastructure) voiced doubts about the deadline.<sup id="cite_ref-frequentbt20130107_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-frequentbt20130107-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2013">2013</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 2013">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>FBB announced on 6 January 2013 that the opening would be further delayed, at least until 2014; however, no definite opening date was given.<sup id="cite_ref-spiegelJan13_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegelJan13-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Klaus Wowereit resigned as chairman of the supervisory board and was replaced by Matthias Platzeck, who previously had served as his deputy. The board also dismissed Rainer Schwarz, the <a href="/wiki/Chief_Executive_Officer" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Executive Officer">CEO</a> of FBB, on 16 January.<sup id="cite_ref-ceofired_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ceofired-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> By January 2013, FBB had announced and cancelled four official opening dates.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_82-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-spiegelJan13_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegelJan13-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> FBB named <a href="/wiki/Hartmut_Mehdorn" title="Hartmut Mehdorn">Hartmut Mehdorn</a>, previously CEO of <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a> (1999\xe2\x80\x932011) and <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a> (2011\xe2\x80\x932013) as Schwarz\'s replacement on 8 March 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-mehdorn_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mehdorn-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Due to the rising passenger numbers at Berlin airports and delays to BER, concerns were voiced in 2013 that the new airport might be too small as passenger numbers at existing Berlin airports were approaching the BER design capacity.<sup id="cite_ref-nyt_82-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2014">2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>On 8 January 2014, FBB announced the airport would not open that year.<sup id="cite_ref-thelocal.de_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thelocal.de-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Mehdorn stated on 24 February 2014 that it was unlikely the airport would open before 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-delay2016_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-delay2016-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> In remarks made in August 2014, he pointed towards 2017 or 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> Mehdorn announced no opening date by 14 October 2014, so a special commission established by the Brandenburg Parliament retained oversight of the project.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Welt15Oct_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Welt15Oct-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-LR15Oct_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LR15Oct-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Schon_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schon-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The initial design for the main hall, known as "the monster" to construction workers, called for a single exhaust system. Revised plans called for multiple systems controlled by 90&#160;km (56&#160;mi) of wiring. By 19 May 2014 <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> had not yet designed the wire harnesses.<sup id="cite_ref-taz666_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-taz666-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> These problems are forcing the initial construction budget to skyrocket.<sup id="cite_ref-spiegelJan13_25-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-spiegelJan13-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BBI sought to open the north pier for use by three to ten flights per day as a test, though other parts of the airport would not be operational for some time. It requested that <i><a href="/wiki/Technischer_%C3%9Cberwachungsverein" title="Technischer \xc3\x9cberwachungsverein">Technischer \xc3\x9cberwachungsverein</a></i> (Technical Inspection Association, T\xc3\x9cV) review the facility for safety and compliance to Brandenburg building codes. In its assessment report issued on 29 July 2014, T\xc3\x9cV found that some lightning rods were missing and that the back-up generator powering the sprinkler system did not provide adequate power. One source with the T\xc3\x9cV stated, "What the airport ordered was sufficient for a circus tent, but [if power fails] not for the dimensions of the terminal."<sup id="cite_ref-bild_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bild-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The 18-kilometre-long (11&#160;mi) exhaust system to remove smoke from a fire was also reported to be leaking.<sup id="cite_ref-leaking_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-leaking-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Citing dissatisfaction with construction progress, members of the airport board indicated during their 8 December 2014 meeting that they were beginning the search for a new CEO, although Mehdorn\'s contract ran through 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-NewChief_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewChief-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> One week later, Mehdorn announced he would resign as soon as the board named a successor, but no later than June 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-resign_121-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-resign-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Karsten M\xc3\xbchlenfeld, former head of Rolls Royce Germany,<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> replaced him as airport CEO in March.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2015">2015</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 2015">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The search for a general planner was eventually stopped in February 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 20 March 2015, Mehdorn again faced questions from the Investigative Commission of Berlin\'s parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-Recover25_126-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Recover25-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-MuhlenfeldStarts_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MuhlenfeldStarts-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> Mehdorn eventually ceased all public duties on 21 May 2015, citing health concerns.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Berlin\'s mayor <a href="/wiki/Michael_M%C3%BCller_(politician,_born_1964)" title="Michael M\xc3\xbcller (politician, born 1964)">Michael M\xc3\xbcller</a> was appointed the new head of the supervisory board (<a href="/wiki/Aufsichtsrat" class="mw-redirect" title="Aufsichtsrat">Aufsichtsrat</a>) on 3 July 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> However, he had disagreements with M\xc3\xbchlenfeld, primarily over the opening date.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Led by Mayor M\xc3\xbcller, the board insisted on an opening in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A former manager for BER was taken into <a href="/wiki/Remand_(detention)" title="Remand (detention)">remand</a> for alleged bribery on 13 May 2015;<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> an <a href="/wiki/Imtech" class="mw-redirect" title="Imtech">Imtech</a> manager was alleged to have given him bribes at a highway gas station in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> Imtech built parts of the fire exhaustion system.\n</p><p>The German branch of (Dutch) Royal Imtech filed for bankruptcy on 6 August 2015,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> and its parent company went bankrupt a few days later.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> As a result, Martin Delius, leader of the commission of inquiry into the failures during the airport\'s construction, stated that the planned opening in late 2017 was doubtful.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Also in August 2015, new allegations of corruption were published in the <a href="/wiki/Bild" title="Bild">Bild</a> newspaper.<sup id="cite_ref-ntv-corruption_142-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ntv-corruption-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> According to the paper, some large contractors filed additional payment demands after completion of their respective projects within BER, and received the complete requested payments with almost no objections. Lawyers reviewing the process stated that the high percentage of claims granted approval was unique and extraordinary. As a result, all payments beginning from the start of the project were to be reviewed.<sup id="cite_ref-ntv-corruption_142-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ntv-corruption-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> The projected opening in 2017 was declared unlikely around the same time.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> At the end of August 2015, though, the new airport head presented the Sch\xc3\xbc\xc3\x9fler plan as the course of action.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> When Mehdorn testified before the Investigations Commission of the Berlin parliament in March 2015, he stated that redesigns to correct the exhaust system would not be completed until "after the summer break," and that the terminal will not be finished until March or April 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-Recover25_126-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Recover25-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>An immediate halt to all construction efforts in the terminal was ordered on 21 September 2015 because a collapse of the main roof was imminent. This was done according to <a href="/wiki/Dahme-Spreewald" title="Dahme-Spreewald">Dahme-Spreewald</a> district\'s construction supervision.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> The shutdown lasted two weeks.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Furthermore, 600 fire protection walls had to be replaced because they were built out of <a href="/wiki/Aerated_concrete" class="mw-redirect" title="Aerated concrete">aerated concrete</a> blocks that provided insufficient fire protection. The mortar was found to be inadequate as well.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2016">2016</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 2016">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>By 2016, further consequences of the low likelihood of a 2017 opening appeared on the horizon. <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tegel_Airport" title="Berlin Tegel Airport">Tegel</a>\'s permit was set to expire at the end of 2017; but if Tegel was closed before BER was opened, massive disruptions would occur due to Tegel handling over 60% of all passenger traffic in Berlin.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> This led to expectations that pressure to open BER would mount drastically.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of 7 February 2016, 24 opaque skylights (which can allow smoke to escape) in the main gangway required approval. The opaque skylights are part of the fire exhaustion system.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> FBB spokesman Daniel Abbou confirmed to <a href="/wiki/Berliner_Morgenpost" title="Berliner Morgenpost">Berliner Morgenpost</a> that the 24 skylights may need "individual approval" rather than a blanket approval for all.<sup id="cite_ref-DiepgenMomper_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DiepgenMomper-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of April 2016, the fire exhaustion system experienced further lapses that would delay a new issuing of the rework permission for the fire suppression system. The underground railway station also needed a redesign for the underground part of the fire exhaustion system. Incoming or departing trains might suck smoke into the station, so air flow guidance was needed to avoid this effect. However, the airport could not decide upon the method by itself, as permission is needed from the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Railway_Authority" title="Federal Railway Authority">Federal Railway Authority</a> (<i>Eisenbahnbundesamt</i>). The construction authority of the district of <a href="/wiki/Dahme-Spreewald" title="Dahme-Spreewald">Dahme-Spreewald</a>, Eisenbahnbundesamt, and the airport thus needed to join in the redesign effort. The plans on how to rebuild the underground part would not be finished before June. Thus, with no plans, the district could not grant the redesign permission. As such, the airport could not start the redesign effort before the beginning of July (assuming that the district would promptly check on the plans). As such, the construction process was delayed by at least 8 months.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> On 17 April 2016, it became clear that the district would conduct an intensive investigation into the construction plans. Airport head M\xc3\xbchlenfeld thus publicly demanded that the parties come to grips with their decision.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Also in April 2016, press spokesman Daniel Abbou was fired after giving "too honest" an interview. He had stated that billions of euros had been squandered, and that only someone "dependent on medication will give you any firm guarantees for this airport."<sup id="cite_ref-PRWeek_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PRWeek-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Abbou_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Abbou-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> On 25 April 2016, M\xc3\xbchlenfeld stated that "surprisingly, demands (towards a simulation of the problem) are higher than expected." In fact, the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Railway_Authority" title="Federal Railway Authority">Federal Railway Authority</a> demanded that the commuter trains be simulated at speeds up to 100 kilometres per hour (62&#160;mph) when entering or leaving the station. This means it would take more time to simulate the exact solution for the underground railway station.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> The Federal Railway Authority also called for the simulation of emergency/evacuation scenarios.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> To prevent suffocation in an emergency, glass towers are to be built inside the railway station that connect to openings in the roof, which will provide fresh air.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mold_(fungus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mold (fungus)">Mold</a> seems to be persistent, the railway station is already ventilated from time to time by mobile fans.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By May 2016, it had become clear that an expedited approval of the underground station would not happen.<sup id="cite_ref-geplatzt_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-geplatzt-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> Because of this, the timetable for opening had to be pushed back to at least 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-rbb-online.de_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rbb-online.de-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Specifically, the airport was unable to conform to the fifth appendix for the construction permission, therefore it was declined. The airport found it disappointing that there was no quick approval of the underground redesign efforts as of 10 June. Instead, the authority stated that a filing for the fifth appendix was incomplete and insufficient. The vice district administrator for Dahme-Spreewald, Chris Halecker, decried political pressure from the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 23 August 2016, a former FBB department head admitted in court to taking \xe2\x82\xac150,000 in bribes from Imtech, on a parking lot next to a highway in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-ntv150000_169-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ntv150000-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> At the end of August 2016 it was announced that the airport had missed an internal deadline, and that the permissions for the next phase of construction could not be issued. This was because the fire protection system for the connection between the airport and railway station lacked sufficient documentation.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> These conditions were met on 6 October 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> The conditions for the final construction approval would only be met on 27 January 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The project management missed a 7 October 2016 deadline to announce a definite opening date for the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> In October 2016, traffic commission chairman Burkert declared that an opening in 2017 was impossible.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> An 11 October 2016 committee session found that motors used to open and close windows would not operate above 30&#160;\xc2\xb0C (86&#160;\xc2\xb0F), necessitating their replacement.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Three thousand smoke detectors went missing, but were later found.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Technical issues involving the electric doors became public on 18 January 2017. It was discovered that 80% of the doors would not open, which created concerns around venting of smoke in a fire.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> The sprinkler system had sustained failures in the south pier.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> The sprinkler heads were replaced for increased water flow, but the pipes were too thin to carry it; as a result the ceiling needed to be opened for the pipes to be replaced.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> The new low-cost terminal T2 will possibly be delayed until after 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> It was revealed in a newspaper report that the airport could not open before 2018, and that this had been known by the airport for three years despite public statements otherwise.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The main construction permit (that is, the permission of the authority of Berlin issues to construction firms) was destined to expire. This would mean all construction work would have to terminate on 23 November 2016. A new law, referred to as a "Lex BER", extended the construction permission for ongoing projects.<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>By the end of 2016, unfinished construction and corrective work indicated clearly that an opening prior to late 2017 was unlikely.<sup id="cite_ref-szOct2013_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-szOct2013-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-buildforever_186-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-buildforever-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> In December 2016, M\xc3\xbchlenfeld hinted at a possible 2018 opening;<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> marketing head Kenny Jacobs suggested March 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2017">2017</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 2017">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In January 2017, it became clear that the airport would not open in 2017,<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup> with some estimates suggesting that the airport would open in 2018 or 2019, at the latest.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> On 6 March 2017, L\xc3\xbctke-Daldrup was appointed to replace M\xc3\xbchlenfeld as the head of the construction project<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> and Rainer Breitschneider was appointed head of the <a href="/wiki/Supervisory_board" title="Supervisory board">supervisory board</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> The target opening was pushed to 2018 or 2019,<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> with
