2020 as a possible option.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> In Aug 2017 the Berliner Zeitung reported that the airport\'s remaining funds would run out in 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of May 2017, estimates suggested the airport could open in late 2018 or early 2019, but an opening in 2020 was not ruled out.<sup id="cite_ref-Tagesspiegel2017_208-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tagesspiegel2017-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> The opening date of 2019 had already been described as ambitious<sup id="cite_ref-Morgenpost2017_209-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Morgenpost2017-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> and even the new opening date of 2020 was called into question. On 23 November 2017, exactly 2,000 days after the originally planned opening date in 2012, a <i><a href="/wiki/Technischer_%C3%9Cberwachungsverein" title="Technischer \xc3\x9cberwachungsverein">T\xc3\x9cV</a></i> report listed additional deficits. It is possible that the new deficits will cause an additional delay of up to two years, with an opening in 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-FAZ2017_210-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAZ2017-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> At the end of 2017, autumn 2020 was announced as the new official opening date.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The recent bankruptcy of <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a> was another problem for the airport. With Air Berlin absent it became even clearer that the airport would not become a major <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hub</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> The number of connections a person can catch would be immediately reduced and Tegel was too far away to be any help in this regard. Interested citizens forced a non-binding public quorum that was held parallel to the federal election, asking whether Tegel should remain open if BER was already in operation. The majority of Berlin\'s citizens agreed.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2017, an audit of the entire airport by Germany\'s technical supervision service <a href="/wiki/T%C3%9CV" class="mw-redirect" title="T\xc3\x9cV">T\xc3\x9cV</a> uncovered more significant lapses in the fire and emergency systems, further pushing back estimates.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2018">2018</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 2018">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In January 2018, it was disclosed that the airport head is <a href="/wiki/Double_dipping" class="mw-redirect" title="Double dipping">simultaneously earning a monthly wage and a retirement pension</a> as a former state secretary of the state of Berlin, a situation described as a "scandal" and potentially illegal.<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup> The airport was scheduled to open in 2020 with a total cost exceeding \xe2\x82\xac7 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> The airport chief executive gave his assurance that the date would be met.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March, it was reported that 750 display screens have already reached the end of their service life and will need to be replaced, as they were switched on for 6 years despite the airport not being open.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Planned extensions of the airport were also seen as a threat to opening in 2020, according to the airport\'s engineering advisor Faulenbach da Costa.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> More people than previously expected would be moving through the main terminal, causing an increase in fire emergency load, with even more passengers arriving through the railway station in the basement. Thus smoke systems would need to be adjusted once again.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> board member <a href="/w/index.php?title=Thorsten_Dirks&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Thorsten Dirks (page does not exist)">Thorsten Dirks</a><span class="noprint" style="font-size:85%; font-style: normal;">&#160;&#91;<a href="https://de.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thorsten_Dirks" class="extiw" title="de:Thorsten Dirks">de</a>&#93;</span> said "the airport will be torn down and rebuilt."<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Personnel changes continued to affect the project, with the head of the technical department J\xc3\xb6rg Marks leaving the company on 19 April 2018, and <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg" title="Brandenburg">Brandenburg</a>\'s state secretary for airport affairs Rainer Bretschneider going into retirement in June.<sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airport failed a <a href="/wiki/Technischer_%C3%9Cberwachungsverein" title="Technischer \xc3\x9cberwachungsverein">mandatory T\xc3\x9cV acceptance test</a> in May 2018, with 863 issues found in the electric wiring.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup> Wiring remained a major issue in 2018. The all-around test was planned to commence sometime in September 2018 but it was postponed to June 2019 because the wiring was still flawed.<sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup> Also in May 2018, <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>, the software supplier for the smoke suction system, testified before Berlin\'s senate\'s airport commission stating that the airport had not yet delivered essential paperwork required for them to complete the suction software.<sup id="cite_ref-230" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> In the same month the airport faced new legal issues as concerned citizens claimed that the aeroplane noise caused by the new airport would violate their rights to be heard. A few months later <a href="/wiki/Bundesverfassungsgericht" class="mw-redirect" title="Bundesverfassungsgericht">Germany\'s supreme court</a> ruled that nighttime flights over BER are lawful.<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June Berlin\'s assembly formed a new committee of inquiry to uncover responsibility for ongoing construction lapses and to investigate possible sources of further delay.<sup id="cite_ref-232" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> The still-unopened airport announced plans to expand with a second terminal in July, with construction to be done by Zechbau Bremen for a total cost of \xe2\x82\xac200 million.<sup id="cite_ref-233" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2019">2019</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 2019">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>It was reported at the start of January 2019 that the construction oversight authority was unwilling to permit the Terminal\'s wiring as is, because it was too tangled.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Berlin\'s <a href="/wiki/Der_Tagesspiegel" title="Der Tagesspiegel">Tagesspiegel</a> reported that Bosch (fire detection) and Caverion (sprinklers) were unwilling to participate in a hearing of Berlin\'s parliament on 14 March 2019. It was then assumed that the airport would not open until 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> The fire protection malfunction seems to be too significant to keep 2020 as an opening date.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 March 2019, it was reported that a software update for the fire alarm system planned to be ready by 29 March would be delayed until late May. T\xc3\x9cV Rheinland warned that there were still considerable problems with the system, and stated that if there were any further delays the October 2020 opening date would be missed.<sup id="cite_ref-2500Tage_237-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2500Tage-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup> On 16 April 2019, the smoke suction system nicknamed "the Monster" finally received approval from T\xc3\x9cV,<sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> afterwards by an expert representing the State.<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In May 2019, it was reported that sand-lime brick used in the foundations of the airport were not sufficiently rated for load, necessitating a costly replacement of much of the underground cabling and reinforced concrete beams. According to a subsequent investigation the problem had been known since 2012. The problematic plastic anchors that were earlier found to be unsuitable for fire were also found not suitable for sand-lime brick. As stated by <a href="/wiki/Deutsches_Institut_f%C3%BCr_Bautechnik" title="Deutsches Institut f\xc3\xbcr Bautechnik">Deutsches Institut f\xc3\xbcr Bautechnik</a>, it is not possible to approve already-installed anchors after the fact.<sup id="cite_ref-Tagesschau9519_240-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tagesschau9519-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> Later in May the head of the airport L\xc3\xbctke-Daldrup stated that "it cannot be guaranteed entirely anymore" that the airport will open in October 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-241" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup> Unapproved screw anchors made of plastic not rated for fire seem to have been the reason for the new delay.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Also known since 2012 were problems with the cable ducts: 700 kilometres (430&#160;mi) of cable needed to be replaced due to water overflow within the cable ducts next to the southern runway. The ducts were not leakproof against incoming water, and had eroded in the decade since they were first installed. The repairs were scheduled to start later in 2019. According to airport head L\xc3\xbctke-Daldrup, the planned opening date of October 2020 was not affected by the cable duct problem, as the repairs could continue while the airport was in operation.<sup id="cite_ref-245" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> German minister of traffic Mr Scheuer however reiterated his concerns that the sand lime brick and cable duct issues could delay the opening beyond 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-246" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> Conservative party member Graeff stated that if the airport continued to see these kinds of delays, then officials should go ahead and start planning construction of a new airport in a different location.<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-248" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The head of the expansion facility management cancelled his contract at the end of June 2019 for unspecified personal reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-249" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> The construction progress at the T2 site remained slow,<sup id="cite_ref-250" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-251" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> but the topping out of T2 finally took place on 30 July.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup> Final equipment tests took place at the airport over the summer of 2019;<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup> with the first tests appearing to have been successful.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 31 July 2019, construction work at terminal T2 was finished in a record time of only 10 months. Initially planned to cost \xe2\x82\xac200 million, the exploding cost of Berlin Brandenburg Airport as a whole made it necessary to reduce standards and cut the cost of T2 by 50%, to no more than \xe2\x82\xac100 million. The attempts to reduce costs were unsuccessful, as criticised in a report to the supervisory board. Nonetheless, L\xc3\xbctke-Daldrup took the timely completion of terminal T2 as a sign that the problems at BER were coming to an end. L\xc3\xbctke-Daldrup said that he was hopeful that the airport could open as soon as August 2020, two months earlier than currently scheduled.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> In late July 2019, L\xc3\xbctke-Daldrup stated that, of the more than 11,000 shortcomings reported in March 2019, over 70% had been resolved, including several hundred problems of high priority that would preclude the start of the final T\xc3\x9cV rehearsal.<sup id="cite_ref-Tagesspiegel_190731_256-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tagesspiegel_190731-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> On 1 August 2019 a several-month T\xc3\x9cV rehearsal of BER\'s technical facilities began, marking the first time that all airport systems have been tested simultaneously.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Renewed checks at T2 yielded serious construction lapses, though. The concrete foundation needed to be partly rebuilt to accommodate technical systems,<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> with issues in the wiring arrangement and the ability to withstand sustained usage and heat.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It was also announced that a third terminal is planned to be erected by 2029<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> and that \xe2\x82\xac174 m for payments to advisors was not listed in the balance sheets for 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> Brandenburg\'s radio station reported that certain tests that were delayed anew at the end of 2019 were what put the opening date of 2020 into doubt again.<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="2020">2020</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 2020">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>In January 2020, union strikes threatened to further delay opening. The union has been fighting for a general working payment to limit competition among ground personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> By mid-February, the planned opening continued to be doubted upon because 5,000 issues still required rectification and certification by an external inspection company (T\xc3\x9cV) in order to complete construction by the end of the first quarter of 2020. These issues were seen as "grave", meaning that any of them could have caused the inspection company to halt operation.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> As of 19&#160;February&#160;2020<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, 1,000 lapses were still unresolved, 3,300 were being checked by T\xc3\x9cV, and 700 proposed solutions had already been rejected. About 70 issues, including the problem of unapproved screw anchors, still lacked the proper documentation to start working on a solution. Those issues threatened to delay the start of test operations that were scheduled for April 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup> The screw anchor problem was resolved in March.<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In early 2020, the airport successfully commenced a volunteer-driven test run of its main functions, including processing at ticket counters.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup> After T\xc3\x9cV approved the emergency and safety systems, the airport received final authority approval on 28 April 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup> Construction work officially ended on 15 May 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Christoph Schaefer was set to become new technical head as a successor to Carsten Wilmsen.<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> The position will remain vacant though due to financial difficulties.<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup> It also has been reported that the airport operations company <a href="/wiki/Flughafen_Berlin_Brandenburg_GmbH" title="Flughafen Berlin Brandenburg GmbH">FBB</a> is in imminent financial trouble due to the construction issues and delays as well as the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Germany" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Germany">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airport finally received its operating licence in May 2020, allowing an opening date to be set.<sup id="cite_ref-license_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-license-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-277" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-278" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> The local and aviation authorities then gave final approval for the airport to open on 31 October 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-finaldate_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finaldate-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Plans to bring forward the closure of Tegel to June 2020 in the wake of the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a> were shelved due to an estimated lack of capacity at Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld\'s old facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From August 2020, the procedure to move all equipment from both current airports to their new facilities commenced.<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 15 October 2020, all test runs of the airport\'s passenger facilities and procedures, which included thousands of volunteers since spring, concluded successfully after being slightly delayed by the COVID-19 pandemic.<sup id="cite_ref-282" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld\'s facilities formally became Terminal 5 of BER ahead on 25 October 2020,<sup id="cite_ref-SXFT5_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SXFT5-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> all airlines moved from Tegel to BER between 31 October and 8 November 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-BERallocations_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BERallocations-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>  The first flight to land at the new airport was an <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a> special service from <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Tegel_Airport" title="Berlin Tegel Airport">Tegel</a> on 31 October 2020, followed shortly after by a <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a> special service from Munich.<sup id="cite_ref-hameja20_284-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hameja20-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup> Lufthansa applied a special "Hauptstadtflieger" (<i>capital city flyer</i>) sticker to the aircraft in celebration of the flight.<sup id="cite_ref-285" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> The first departure from the new Terminal 1 was a flight to <a href="/wiki/Heathrow_Airport" title="Heathrow Airport">London\xe2\x80\x93Heathrow</a> on 1 November 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-286" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminals">Terminals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Terminals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BER_Terminals.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/BER_Terminals.png/220px-BER_Terminals.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="159" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/BER_Terminals.png/330px-BER_Terminals.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/BER_Terminals.png/440px-BER_Terminals.png 2x" data-file-width="2500" data-file-height="1806" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BER_Terminals.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Terminal layout including the newly added Terminal 2 as well as Terminal 5, the former Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:120513-BER-Flugbr%C3%BCcken.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/120513-BER-Flugbr%C3%BCcken.JPG/220px-120513-BER-Flugbr%C3%BCcken.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/120513-BER-Flugbr%C3%BCcken.JPG/330px-120513-BER-Flugbr%C3%BCcken.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/120513-BER-Flugbr%C3%BCcken.JPG/440px-120513-BER-Flugbr%C3%BCcken.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2176" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:120513-BER-Flugbr%C3%BCcken.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main pier of Terminal 1</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_brandenburg_airport_terminal_1_-_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Berlin_brandenburg_airport_terminal_1_-_3.jpg/220px-Berlin_brandenburg_airport_terminal_1_-_3.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Berlin_brandenburg_airport_terminal_1_-_3.jpg/330px-Berlin_brandenburg_airport_terminal_1_-_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Berlin_brandenburg_airport_terminal_1_-_3.jpg/440px-Berlin_brandenburg_airport_terminal_1_-_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6720" data-file-height="4480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_brandenburg_airport_terminal_1_-_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The main hall of Terminal 1</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_1">Terminal 1</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Terminal 1">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The U-shaped main terminal building of Berlin Brandenburg Airport, named <b>Terminal 1</b> and consisting of sections <b>A</b>, <b>B (01-25)</b>, <b>C</b> and <b>D</b> was designed by <a href="/wiki/Gerkan,_Marg_and_Partners" title="Gerkan, Marg and Partners">gmp</a> architects. They are the same company which designed the hexagonal Terminal A at Tegel Airport which opened in 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-287" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> At BER the terminal sits between the two runways, creating a so-called <i>midfield airport</i> above the underground train station. The terminal has four public levels designated 0, 1, 2 and 3.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Airport_check-in" title="Airport check-in">check-in area</a> is located in the public area at Level 1 and houses 118 counters organised in eight clusters, called <i>check-in isles</i>. Planners anticipate that a significant number of passengers will use the more than 100 self check-in machines that will be installed. Additionally, by May 2015 two extensions had been added to both sides of the main check-in area containing 12 more check-in counters and eight security lanes each to avoid overcrowding of the main hall.<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airside area will be accessible only to ticketed and <a href="/wiki/Airport_security" title="Airport security">screened</a> passengers. <a href="/wiki/Securitas_(Swedish_security_company)" class="mw-redirect" title="Securitas (Swedish security company)">Securitas Germany</a> will staff the 35 screening stations. BER is equipped with 25 <a href="/wiki/Jet_bridge" title="Jet bridge">jet bridges</a> with another 85 aircraft stands on the apron. The boarding and arrival areas are divided into three piers with the main pier 715 metres (2,350&#160;ft) long and the north and south piers at 350 metres (1,150&#160;ft) each. The main pier contains 16 jet-bridges, all but one have two levels, thus separating arriving and departing passengers. Level 1 is intended for <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">Schengen passengers</a> (gates A01\xe2\x80\x93A20, B01\xe2\x80\x93B20), while Level 2 (gates C01\xe2\x80\x93C19, D01\xe2\x80\x93D17) is for non-Schengen passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-presskit_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-presskit-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>8\xe2\x80\x9310</span></sup>  Eight of the gates can accommodate <a href="/wiki/Wide-body_aircraft" title="Wide-body aircraft">wide-body aircraft</a> and one gate has been designed to accommodate the <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A380" title="Airbus A380">Airbus A380</a>. The apron has sufficient space to allow installation of a dual jetway allowing a quick boarding and disembarking process. A mezzanine (Level Z) at gates A21\xe2\x80\x9322 and B21 allows for additional pre-boarding security checks for high-risk flights to the United States and <a href="/wiki/Israel" title="Israel">Israel</a>. Lufthansa and <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>/<a href="/wiki/KLM" title="KLM">KLM</a> will operate <a href="/wiki/Airport_lounge" title="Airport lounge">airport lounges</a> in the main pier which will also be open for passengers of the respective <a href="/wiki/Airline_alliance" title="Airline alliance">alliance partners</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Handbuch_289-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Handbuch-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The south pier was reserved for near-exclusive use of defunct <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a> and its <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a> partners. The south terminal contains nine single-storey jet bridges (gates A30\xe2\x80\x93A38). The north pier features a more minimalist design compared to the other two piers. This is to meet the demands of <a href="/wiki/Low-cost_carrier" title="Low-cost carrier">low-cost carriers</a> and has no jetbridges, but boarding gates (B30\xe2\x80\x9345) with direct apron access.<sup id="cite_ref-Handbuch_289-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Handbuch-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Major operators at Terminal 1 are <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa_Group" title="Lufthansa Group">Lufthansa Group</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a>, <a href="/wiki/British_Airways" title="British Airways">British Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Turkish_Airlines" title="Turkish Airlines">Turkish Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_Airlines" title="United Airlines">United Airlines</a> and <a href="/wiki/Qatar_Airways" title="Qatar Airways">Qatar Airways</a> amongst others.<sup id="cite_ref-airlinelocations_290-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airlinelocations-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_2">Terminal 2</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Terminal 2">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Plans for a separate low-cost airline terminal costing \xe2\x82\xac200 million were released in March 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> Construction for the now named <b>Terminal 2</b> with section <b>B (30\xe2\x80\x9345)</b> (which was originally constructed as part of Terminal 1) began in 2018 and finished in time in September 2020 to provide further capacity especially for low-cost carriers \xe2\x80\x93 <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a> is supposed to operate their Berlin base out of Terminal 2.<sup id="cite_ref-TST2_292-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TST2-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> However, due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, the facility remains closed for the time being as the capacity is not needed for the foreseeable future.<sup id="cite_ref-TST2_292-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TST2-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Terminal 2 is constructed as a more basic departures and arrivals facility next to the Terminal 1 main building, directly connected with its northern pier to gain more check-in capacity while sharing the same airside areas.<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Besides Eurowings, Terminal 2 will be mainly used by <a href="/wiki/Wizz_Air" title="Wizz Air">Wizz Air</a> alongside <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_Air_Shuttle" title="Norwegian Air Shuttle">Norwegian Air Shuttle</a> and others after its opening. Until then, those are handled in Terminals 1 and 5 for the time being.<sup id="cite_ref-airlinelocations_290-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airlinelocations-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Terminal_5">Terminal 5</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Terminal 5">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><b>Terminal 5</b> was made up of the former terminal facilities of old <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Sch%C3%B6nefeld_Airport" title="Berlin Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport">Berlin Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport</a> which were refurbished and renamed from sections A, B, C, and D to <b>K</b>, <b>L</b>, <b>M</b>, and <b>Q</b>, respectively. In 2019, it was decided to leave the old facilities operational to provide more capacity for the expected passenger crowds.<sup id="cite_ref-294" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> The old tarmac at Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld, which was refurbished and upgraded, was also used.<sup id="cite_ref-296" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Terminal 5 was scheduled to be operated until the inauguration of the planned Terminal 3 by 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-terminal3_298-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-terminal3-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> However, in November 2020, it was announced that Terminal 5 would be shut down for the time being due to low passenger numbers in the wake of the COVID-19 pandemic, with all flights relocating to the main Terminal 1.<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup> The terminal was closed on February 22, 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-march-covid-passenger-shortage_300-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-march-covid-passenger-shortage-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> It is considered likely that it will never open again.<sup id="cite_ref-march-covid-passenger-shortage_300-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-march-covid-passenger-shortage-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Terminal 5, which was located to the north side of the airport, was connected with the central areas of the airport (Terminals 1 and 2) solely landside by the S-Bahn between the new airport station and <a href="/wiki/Flughafen_BER_-_Terminal_5_station" class="mw-redirect" title="Flughafen BER - Terminal 5 station">the old station which formerly served Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport_overview">Airport overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Airport overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:393px;max-width:393px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:EDDB_BER_Layout.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/EDDB_BER_Layout.png/200px-EDDB_BER_Layout.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="141" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/EDDB_BER_Layout.png/300px-EDDB_BER_Layout.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/EDDB_BER_Layout.png/400px-EDDB_BER_Layout.png 2x" data-file-width="2800" data-file-height="1980" /></a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:187px;max-width:187px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Map_Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Map_Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport.png/185px-Map_Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport.png" decoding="async" width="185" height="141" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Map_Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport.png/278px-Map_Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0b/Map_Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport.png/370px-Map_Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport.png 2x" data-file-width="2800" data-file-height="2141" /></a></div></div></div><div class="trow" style="display:flex"><div class="thumbcaption">Current and planned layout of the airport, November 2020</div></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Airport_berlin_BER_2019.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Airport_berlin_BER_2019.jpg/220px-Airport_berlin_BER_2019.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Airport_berlin_BER_2019.jpg/330px-Airport_berlin_BER_2019.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Airport_berlin_BER_2019.jpg/440px-Airport_berlin_BER_2019.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4269" data-file-height="2846" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Airport_berlin_BER_2019.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Aerial view</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Runways">Runways</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Runways">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Berlin Brandenburg Airport has two parallel runways. With a spacing of 1,900 metres (6,200&#160;ft), this allows independent flight operations without interference from <a href="/wiki/Wake_turbulence" title="Wake turbulence">wake turbulence</a>.\n</p><p>The northern runway of BER is the southern runway of the old Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport and has been in use since the 1960s. To adapt it for the new airport, it has been renovated and lengthened from 3,000 to 3,600 metres (9,800 to 12,000&#160;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> The newly built southern runway has a length of 4,000 metres (13,000&#160;ft) and was officially commissioned on 31 May 2012. Blackouts of the runway <a href="/wiki/Beacon" title="Beacon">beacon</a> of the southern runway led to investigations concerning air traffic safety.<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>BER covers 1,470 <a href="/wiki/Hectare" title="Hectare">hectares</a> (3,632 acres) of land.<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_traffic_control">Air traffic control</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Air traffic control">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_brandenburg_airport_tower.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Berlin_brandenburg_airport_tower.jpg/220px-Berlin_brandenburg_airport_tower.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Berlin_brandenburg_airport_tower.jpg/330px-Berlin_brandenburg_airport_tower.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Berlin_brandenburg_airport_tower.jpg/440px-Berlin_brandenburg_airport_tower.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4295" data-file-height="6443" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Berlin_brandenburg_airport_tower.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Air traffic control tower</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Flugsicherung" title="Deutsche Flugsicherung">Deutsche Flugsicherung</a> is responsible for <a href="/wiki/Air_traffic_control" title="Air traffic control">air traffic control</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airport_apron" title="Airport apron">apron control</a> at Berlin Brandenburg Airport. At 72 metres (240&#160;ft), the control tower is the third highest in Germany (only surpassed by <a href="/wiki/Munich_Airport" title="Munich Airport">Munich Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/D%C3%BCsseldorf_Airport" title="D\xc3\xbcsseldorf Airport">D\xc3\xbcsseldorf Airport</a>). On 25 March 2012, the new tower opened replacing the former facility at Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld.<sup id="cite_ref-toweropening_305-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-toweropening-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup> Technical control (power supply and IT) went into operation on 16 March 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cargo_and_general_aviation">Cargo and general aviation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Cargo and general aviation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The initial module of the midfield cargo facilities has a capacity of 60&#160;thousand tonnes (130&#160;million pounds) of cargo per year. With the completion of all planned expansions this could handle up to 600&#160;thousand tonnes (1.3&#160;billion pounds) per year. The <a href="/wiki/General_aviation" title="General aviation">general aviation</a> terminal is located in the northern part of BER.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport_tourism_facilities">Airport tourism facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Airport tourism facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The <i>Infotower</i> was a 32-metre (105&#160;ft) observation tower located adjacent to the northern cargo terminal that included a museum and a gift shop. It was closed and demolished in 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> FBB also offers guided tours of the airport which have grown in popularity since the delayed opening.<sup id="cite_ref-infotower_308-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-infotower-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt20140410_309-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt20140410-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aircraft_maintenance">Aircraft maintenance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Aircraft maintenance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The two large hangars at BER were to be used by Lufthansa and Air Berlin respectively. However, Air Berlin have ceased operations as of 28 October 2017. Both provide enough space for maintenance work on four to five <a href="/wiki/Narrow-body_aircraft" title="Narrow-body aircraft">narrow-body aircraft</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-hangar_310-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hangar-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-airliners_311-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airliners-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_use">Government use</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Government use">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The air transport wing of the <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_of_Defence_(Germany)" title="Federal Ministry of Defence (Germany)">German Defence Ministry</a> (<i>Flugbereitschaft</i>) responsible for government flights will move large parts of its operations to Berlin Brandenburg Airport from its still-current base at <a href="/wiki/Cologne_Bonn_Airport" title="Cologne Bonn Airport">Cologne Bonn Airport</a> near Germany\'s former capital <a href="/wiki/Bonn" title="Bonn">Bonn</a>. It operates a fleet of <a href="/wiki/Bombardier_Global_Express" title="Bombardier Global Express">Bombardier Global Express</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A319" title="Airbus A319">Airbus A319</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A321" title="Airbus A321">Airbus A321</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A340-300" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A340-300">Airbus A340-300</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350-900" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350-900">Airbus A350-900</a> VIP-configured aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-airfleets_312-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-airfleets-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> However Cologne/Bonn will remain the home base of the government fleet for the time being.<sup id="cite_ref-govterm_313-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govterm-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Institute_for_Federal_Real_Estate_(Germany)" title="Institute for Federal Real Estate (Germany)">Institute for Federal Real Estate</a> has been planning to construct a terminal on the northern edge of the airport for use by government officials and to welcome foreign dignitaries during <a href="/wiki/State_visit" title="State visit">state visits</a>. The former Terminal A of Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport was planned to serve as an interim terminal until the new building was to be finished.<sup id="cite_ref-ulrichpaul_314-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ulrichpaul-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-schoelkopf_315-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-schoelkopf-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> However, in March 2016 the management of the airport terminated the contract with the German government that guaranteed usage of Terminal A of Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport upon the completion of BER for the area to be used for a different purpose. The termination was disputed between airport officials and the German <a href="/wiki/Federal_Ministry_of_Transport_and_Digital_Infrastructure" title="Federal Ministry of Transport and Digital Infrastructure">Federal Ministry of Transport and Digital Infrastructure</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>M\xc3\xbchlenfeld suggested a provisional ramp area west of Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld\'s main terminal as a replacement solution and construction site for an interim government terminal at the end of February 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup> This then supposed interim government terminal was finished at a cost of around \xe2\x82\xac70 million while the permanent government terminal was planned to begin operations around 2025, at a cost of additionally around \xe2\x82\xac344 million, which left its completion in doubt.<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup> In December 2019, the German government cancelled all plans to construct a more representative facility until at least 2030.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The government terminal was inaugurated and put in use on 21 October 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-govterm_313-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-govterm-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operating_hours">Operating hours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Operating hours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Noise abatement regulations in the airport\'s operating licence mean no takeoffs or landings are allowed between midnight and 05:00. The <a href="/wiki/Federal_Administrative_Court_of_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Federal Administrative Court of Germany">Federal Administrative Court of Germany</a> rejected a lawsuit by residents aiming to extend this night flight ban from 23:00 to 06:00 on 13 October 2011. It was also ruled that affected residents should be provided with additional noise insulation.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Projected_passenger_volume_and_expansion_plans">Projected passenger volume and expansion plans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Projected passenger volume and expansion plans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Since German reunification, air traffic in Berlin has grown greatly. In 1991, the combined passenger volume of the city\'s airports was at 7.9 million per year. By 2014, this number had risen to 28 million.<sup id="cite_ref-ADVtraffic_321-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ADVtraffic-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup> By Berlin Brandenburg\'s opening, it was projected to have a capacity of 27 million passengers per year.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg_322-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup> There are concerns that the airport will have insufficient capacity upon opening and plans are already in place for expansion.<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup> It may be expanded by up to two satellite concourses, bringing the terminal capacity to 45 million with runways capable of accommodating 50 million passengers per year. The two satellites located on the apron parallel to the main pier and linked by tunnel, are included in the <a href="/wiki/Construction_permit" class="mw-redirect" title="Construction permit">construction permit</a> of Berlin Brandenburg Airport. This means they could be built at any time without further regulatory hurdles or the possibility of third-party objections. A possible third runway could be located in the south, though no such plans exist to date.<sup id="cite_ref-Berliner_Flughafen-Gesellschaft_mbH_324-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Berliner_Flughafen-Gesellschaft_mbH-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Airlines_and_destinations">Airlines and destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Airlines and destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Major_operators">Major operators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Major operators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As of summer 2020, <a href="/wiki/EasyJet" title="EasyJet">easyJet</a> was due to become the overall largest airline at BER in terms of routes served, ahead of <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a>. In May 2019, Ryanair announced that they would not move to the new facilities, and would keep using the old building at the side of Berlin Sch\xc3\xb6nefeld Airport, which has now become part of Berlin Brandenburg Airport as its Terminal 5.<sup id="cite_ref-325" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-325">&#91;325&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Until its demise, <a href="/wiki/Air_Berlin" title="Air Berlin">Air Berlin</a> had planned to move its primary <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">hub</a> from Tegel to Berlin Brandenburg. As a member of the <a href="/wiki/Oneworld" title="Oneworld">Oneworld</a> <a href="/wiki/Airline_alliance" title="Airline alliance">airline alliance</a>, Air Berlin required airport facilities capable of meeting the demands of its connecting passengers that Tegel could not provide. However, Air Berlin filed for <a href="/wiki/Insolvency" title="Insolvency">insolvency</a> on 15 August 2017 and large parts of it were bought by <a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, Germany\'s largest airline, ahead of its collapse on the 27th of that month.<sup id="cite_ref-n-tv.de_326-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-n-tv.de-326">&#91;326&#93;</a></sup> Airport head L\xc3\xbctke-Daldrup declared on 16 September 2017 that the bankruptcy of Air Berlin would have no imminent impact on the expected traffic flow volume at the new airport<sup id="cite_ref-327" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-327">&#91;327&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-328" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-328">&#91;328&#93;</a></sup> as several of Air Berlin\'s routes had been merged into other companies.<sup id="cite_ref-329" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-329">&#91;329&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Lufthansa" title="Lufthansa">Lufthansa</a>, however, does not use Berlin Brandenburg Airport as a hub.<sup id="cite_ref-330" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-330">&#91;330&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-331" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-331">&#91;331&#93;</a></sup> By 2011, Lufthansa planned to greatly expand its presence in Berlin. At its interim facilities at Tegel Airport the airline added several European destinations <sup id="cite_ref-LHgrowing_332-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LHgrowing-332">&#91;332&#93;</a></sup> which have all since ceased or were handed over to <a href="/wiki/Eurowings" title="Eurowings">Eurowings</a>.\n</p><p>It remains unclear if all of the few long-haul routes to and from Berlin will resume anytime soon after the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>. As of summer 2020, eight destinations in the <a href="/wiki/US" class="mw-redirect" title="US">US</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> were served.<sup id="cite_ref-333" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-333">&#91;333&#93;</a></sup> However, <a href="/wiki/Scoot" title="Scoot">Scoot</a> cancelled their year-round service to <a href="/wiki/Singapore_Changi_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Singapore Changi Airport">Singapore</a> until at least summer 2021<sup id="cite_ref-334" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-334">&#91;334&#93;</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines" title="American Airlines">American Airlines</a> terminated their seasonal route from Berlin to <a href="/wiki/Philadelphia_International_Airport" title="Philadelphia International Airport">Philadelphia</a> altogether<sup id="cite_ref-335" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-335">&#91;335&#93;</a></sup> followed by <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a>\' seasonal service to <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_International_Airport" title="John F. Kennedy International Airport">New York JFK</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-336" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-336">&#91;336&#93;</a></sup> leaving the airport with even fewer long-haul connections.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Passenger">Passenger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Berlin_Brandenburg_Airport&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Passenger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The following airlines operate regular scheduled and charter flights at Berlin Brandenburg Airport:<sup id="cite_ref-337" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-337">&#91;337&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable" style="font-size:95%"><tbody><tr><th>Airlines</th><th class="unsortable">Destinations</th></tr><tr><td> <a href="/wiki/Aegean_Airlines" title="Aegean Airlines">Aegean Airlines</a> </td><td> <a href="/wiki/Athens_International_Airport" title="Athens International Airport">Athens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thessaloniki_Airport" title="Thessaloniki Airport">Thessaloniki</a> (begins 13 June 2021)<sup id="cite_ref-A3S21_338-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A3S21-338">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup> <br /><b>Seasonal:</b> <a href="/wiki/Heraklion_International_Airport" title="Heraklion International Airport">Heraklion</a> (begins 2 June 2021)<sup id="cite_ref-A3S21_338-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A3S21-338">&#91;338&#93;</a></sup> \n</td></tr><tr><td>
